<p><b>Montserrat</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɒ/ short 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> island—specifically in the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>, which is part of the chain known as the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a> (BOT). Montserrat measures approximately 16 km (10 mi) long and 11 km (7 mi) wide, with approximately 40 km (25 mi) of coastline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Montserrat is nicknamed <i>The Emerald Isle of the Caribbean</i> both for its resemblance to coastal <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> and for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_ancestry" title="Irish ancestry">Irish ancestry</a> of many of its inhabitants.</p>
<p>On 18 July 1995, the previously <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dormant_volcano" title="Dormant volcano">dormant</a> <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re_Hills" title="Soufrière Hills">Soufrière Hills</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a>, in the southern part of the island, became active. Eruptions destroyed Montserrat's <a href="/wiki/Georgian_era" title="Georgian era">Georgian era</a> capital city of <a href="/wiki/Plymouth,_Montserrat" title="Plymouth, Montserrat">Plymouth</a>. Between 1995 and 2000, two-thirds of the island's population was forced to flee, primarily to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, leaving fewer than 1,200 people on the island as of 1997 (rising to nearly 5,000 by 2016).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016Pop_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-2016Pop-4">[4]</a></sup> The volcanic activity continues, mostly affecting the vicinity of Plymouth, including its docking facilities, and the eastern side of the island around the former <a href="/wiki/W._H._Bramble_Airport" title="W. H. Bramble Airport">W. H. Bramble Airport</a>, the remnants of which were buried by flows from volcanic activity on 11 February 2010.</p>
<p>An exclusion zone that extends from the south coast of the island north to parts of the Belham Valley was imposed because of the size of the existing volcanic dome and the resulting potential for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyroclastics" title="Pyroclastics">pyroclastic</a> activity. Visitors are generally not permitted entry into the exclusion zone, but an impressive view of the destruction of Plymouth can be seen from the top of Garibaldi Hill in Isles Bay. Relatively quiet since early 2010, the volcano continues to be closely monitored by the <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_Volcano_Observatory" title="Montserrat Volcano Observatory">Montserrat Volcano Observatory</a>. It is the most studied volcano in the world and Montserrat is regarded as a 'Modern Day Pompeii' in the Caribbean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Montserrat is also home to the Montserrat Yachting Association.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>A new town and port is being developed at Little Bay, which is on the northwest coast of the island. While this construction proceeds, the centre of government and businesses rests at <a href="/wiki/Brades" title="Brades">Brades</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1493, Christopher Columbus named the island <i>Santa Maria de Montserrate</i>, after the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_of_Montserrat" title="Virgin of Montserrat">Virgin of Montserrat</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_de_Montserrat" title="Santa Maria de Montserrat">Monastery of Montserrat</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_(mountain)" title="Montserrat (mountain)">Montserrat mountain</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> in <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> "Montserrat" means "<a href="/wiki/Serration" title="Serration">serrated</a> mountain" in <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1791" data-file-width="1791" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif/220px-Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif/330px-Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif/440px-Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Little_Bay_from_above,_Montserrat.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG/220px-Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG/330px-Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG/440px-Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Little_Bay_from_above,_Montserrat.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A view of half of the coastline of Little Bay, and a glimpse of Carrs Bay, taken from partway up the headland between Little Bay and Rendezvous Bay, 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Archaeological field work in 2012, in Montserrat's Centre Hills indicated there was an Archaic (pre-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" title="Arawak peoples">Arawak</a>) occupation between 4000 and 2500 <a href="/wiki/Before_Present" title="Before Present">BP</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Later coastal sites show the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Saladoid" title="Saladoid">Saladoid</a> culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 1493, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> passed Montserrat in his <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus#Caribbean_exploration" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">second voyage</a>, after being told that the island was unoccupied due to raids by the <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>A number of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Irishmen</a> settled in Montserrat in 1642.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colonial_Law.27_1966._P._855_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Law.27_1966._P._855-12">[12]</a></sup> The preponderance of Irish in the first wave of European settlers led a leading legal scholar to remark that a "nice question" is whether the original settlers took with them the law of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Kingdom of Ireland</a> insofar as it differed from the law of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The island was captured by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">French</a> in 1666.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colonial_Law.27_1966._P._855_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Law.27_1966._P._855-12">[12]</a></sup> It was captured shortly afterwards by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> and English control of the island was confirmed under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Breda_(1667)" title="Treaty of Breda (1667)">Treaty of Breda</a> the following year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colonial_Law.27_1966._P._855_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Law.27_1966._P._855-12">[12]</a></sup> Despite the interruption to English rule, the island's legal status is that of a colony acquired by settlement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colonial_Law.27_1966._P._855_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Law.27_1966._P._855-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neofeudalism" title="Neofeudalism">neo-feudal</a> colony developed amongst the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Redlegs" title="Redlegs">redlegs</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (April 2014)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The colonists began to transport <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">Sub-Saharan African</a> slaves for labour, as was common to most <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> islands. The colonists built an economy based on the production of sugar, <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">rum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arrowroot" title="Arrowroot">arrowroot</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_island_cotton" title="Sea island cotton">sea island cotton</a>, cultivated on large plantations manned by slave labour. By the late 18th century, numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plantations" title="Plantations">plantations</a> had been developed on the island. Many Irish continued to be transported to the island, to work as indentured servants; some were exiled during the English <a href="/wiki/Cromwellian_conquest_of_Ireland" title="Cromwellian conquest of Ireland">Cromwellian conquest of Ireland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-everyculture_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-everyculture-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century">18th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 18th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 17 March 1768, slaves rebelled but failed to achieve freedom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The people of Montserrat celebrate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Patrick%27s_Day" title="St Patrick's Day">St Patrick's Day</a> as a public holiday due to the slave revolt. Festivities held that week commemorate the culture of Montserrat in song, dance, food and traditional costumes.</p>
<p>In 1782, during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, France <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_capture_of_Montserrat" title="French capture of Montserrat">briefly captured</a> Montserrat after supporting the American rebels. The French returned the island to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">1783 Treaty of Paris</a>, which ended that conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Irish_language_in_Montserrat">Irish language in Montserrat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Irish language in Montserrat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Irish constituted the largest proportion of the white population from the founding of the colony in 1628. Many were indentured labourers; others were merchants or plantation owners. The geographer Thomas Jeffrey claimed in <i>The West India Atlas</i> (1780) that the majority of those on Montserrat were either Irish or of Irish descent, “so that the use of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish language</a> is preserved on the island, even among the Negroes”.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>African slaves and Irish colonists of all classes were in constant contact, with sexual relationships being common and a population of mixed descent appearing as a consequence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The Irish were also prominent in Caribbean commerce, with their merchants importing Irish goods such as beef, pork, butter and herring, and also importing slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is indirect evidence that the use of the Irish language continued in Montserrat until at least the middle of the nineteenth century. The <a href="/wiki/County_Kilkenny" title="County Kilkenny">Kilkenny</a> diarist and Irish scholar <a href="/wiki/Amhlaoibh_%C3%93_S%C3%BAilleabh%C3%A1in" title="Amhlaoibh Ó Súilleabháin">Amhlaoibh Ó Súilleabháin</a> noted in 1831 that he had heard that Irish was still spoken in Montserrat by both black and white inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-De_Bhaldraithe_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-De_Bhaldraithe-21">[21]</a></sup> A letter by W.F. Butler in <i>The Atheneum</i> (15 July 1905) quotes an account by a <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a> civil servant, C. Cremen, of what he had heard from a retired sailor called John O’Donovan, a fluent Irish speaker:</p>
<dl>
<dd><i>He frequently told me that in the year 1852, when mate of the brig Kaloolah, he went ashore on the island of Montserrat which was then out of the usual track of shipping. He said he was much surprised to hear the negroes actually talking Irish among themselves, and that he joined in the conversation…</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-De_Bhaldraithe_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-De_Bhaldraithe-21">[21]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p>There is no evidence for the survival of the Irish language in Montserrat into the twentieth century.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_crops_and_politics">New crops and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: New crops and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Britain <a href="/wiki/Slavery_Abolition_Act_1833" title="Slavery Abolition Act 1833">abolished slavery</a> in Montserrat and its other Caribbean territories effective August 1834.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the nineteenth century, falling sugar-prices had an adverse effect on the island's economy, as <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and other nations competed in the trade.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1857, the British philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Sturge" title="Joseph Sturge">Joseph Sturge</a> bought a sugar estate to prove it was economically viable to employ paid labour rather than slaves. Numerous members of the Sturge family bought additional land. In 1869 the family established the Montserrat Company Limited and planted lime trees, started the commercial production of lime juice, set up a school, and sold parcels of land to the inhabitants of the island. Much of Montserrat came to be owned by <a href="/wiki/Smallholding" title="Smallholding">smallholders</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Connection_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Connection-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 1871 to 1958, Montserrat was administered as part of the federal <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown colony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Leeward_Islands" title="British Leeward Islands">British Leeward Islands</a>, becoming a province of the short-lived <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> from 1958 to 1962.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1979, <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> producer <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a>’s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIR_Studios" title="AIR Studios">AIR Studios Montserrat</a> opened. The island attracted world-famous musicians, who came to record in the peaceful and lush tropical surroundings of Montserrat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The last decade of the twentieth century, however, brought two events that devastated the island.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_Island_Sunset_(4568325551).jpg"><img alt="Montserrat Island Sunset (4568325551).jpg" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1174" data-file-width="1739" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg/220px-Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg/330px-Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg/440px-Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_Island_Sunset_(4568325551).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the early hours of 17 September 1989, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">Hurricane Hugo</a>, a Category 5 storm, struck Montserrat with full force, producing sustained winds of 297 kilometres per hour (185 mph). It damaged more than 90 percent of the structures on the island. AIR Studios closed, and the tourist economy was virtually wiped out. Within a few years, the island had recovered considerably, only to be damaged again, and even more severely, six years later by volcanic activity that started in 1995.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coastal_cliffs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="480" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Coastal_cliffs.jpg/220px-Coastal_cliffs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Coastal_cliffs.jpg/330px-Coastal_cliffs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Coastal_cliffs.jpg/440px-Coastal_cliffs.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coastal_cliffs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Montserrat's coastline</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Montserrat" title="Geography of Montserrat">Geography of Montserrat</a></div>
<p>The island of Montserrat is approximately 480 km (300 mi) east-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and 48 km (30 mi) southwest of <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>. The island lies north-northwest of <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> (France). It comprises 104 km<sup>2</sup> (40 sq mi) and is gradually increasing owing to the buildup of volcanic deposits on the southeast coast. The island is 16 km (9.9 mi) long and 11 km (6.8 mi) wide, with rock cliffs rising 15 to 30 m (49 to 98 ft) above the sea and a number of smooth bottomed sandy beaches scattered among <a href="/wiki/Cove" title="Cove">coves</a> on the western (Caribbean) side of the island.</p>
<p>Montserrat has two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islets" title="Islets">islets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Redonda" title="Kingdom of Redonda">Kingdom of Redonda</a> and Virgin, as well as Statue Rock.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Volcano_and_exclusion_zone">Volcano and exclusion zone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Volcano and exclusion zone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_eruption.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="800" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Montserrat_eruption.JPG/220px-Montserrat_eruption.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Montserrat_eruption.JPG/330px-Montserrat_eruption.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Montserrat_eruption.JPG/440px-Montserrat_eruption.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_eruption.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Plymouth,_Montserrat" title="Plymouth, Montserrat">Plymouth</a>, the former capital city and major port of Montserrat on 12 July 1997, after <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_flow" title="Pyroclastic flow">pyroclastic flows</a> burned much of what was not covered in ash.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In July 1995, Montserrat's <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re_Hills" title="Soufrière Hills">Soufrière Hills</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a>, dormant for centuries, erupted and soon buried the island's capital, Plymouth, in more than 12 metres (39 ft) of mud, destroyed its airport and docking facilities, and rendered the southern part of the island, now termed the exclusion zone, uninhabitable and not safe for travel. The southern part of the island was evacuated and visits are severely restricted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The exclusion zone also includes two sea areas adjacent to the land areas of most volcanic activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the destruction of Plymouth and disruption of the economy, more than half of the population left the island, which also lacked housing. During the late 1990s, additional eruptions occurred. On 25 June 1997, a pyroclastic flow travelled down Mosquito Ghaut. This <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_surge" title="Pyroclastic surge">pyroclastic surge</a> could not be restrained by the ghaut and spilled out of it, killing 19 people who were in the (officially evacuated) Streatham village area. Several others in the area suffered severe burns.</p>
<p>For a number of years in the early 2000s, the volcano's activity consisted mostly of infrequent ventings of <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash" title="Volcanic ash">ash</a> into the uninhabited areas in the south. The ash falls occasionally extended into the northern and western parts of the island. In the most recent period of increased activity at the Soufrière Hills volcano, from November 2009 through February 2010, ash vented and there was a <a href="/wiki/Vulcanian_eruption" title="Vulcanian eruption">vulcanian explosion</a> that sent <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_flow" title="Pyroclastic flow">pyroclastic flows</a> down several sides of the mountain. Travel into parts of the exclusion zone is occasionally allowed, though only by a licence from the Royal Montserrat Police Force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The northern part of Montserrat has barely been affected by volcanic activity, and remains lush and green. In February 2005, <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal" title="Anne, Princess Royal">The Princess Royal</a> officially opened what is now called the <a href="/wiki/John_A._Osborne_Airport" title="John A. Osborne Airport">John A. Osborne Airport</a> in the north. Since 2011, it handles several flights daily operated by <a href="/wiki/FlyMontserrat" title="FlyMontserrat">Fly Montserrat Airways</a>. Docking facilities are in place at Little Bay, where the new capital town is being constructed; the new government centre is at Brades, a short distance away.</p>
<p>In recognition of the disaster, in 1998, the people of Montserrat were granted full residency rights in the United Kingdom, allowing them to migrate if they chose. British citizenship was granted in 2002.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Montserrat" title="List of birds of Montserrat">List of birds of Montserrat</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Montserrat" title="List of mammals of Montserrat">List of mammals of Montserrat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_amphibians_and_reptiles_of_Montserrat" title="List of amphibians and reptiles of Montserrat">List of amphibians and reptiles of Montserrat</a></div>
<p>Montserrat, like many isolated islands, is home to some exceptionally rare plant and animal species. Work undertaken by the Montserrat National Trust in collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanic_Gardens,_Kew" title="Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew">Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew</a> has centred on the conservation of pribby (<i>Rondeletia buxifolia</i>) in the Centre Hills region. Until 2006, this species was known only from one book about the vegetation of Montserrat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In 2006, conservationists also rescued several plants of the endangered Montserrat orchid (<i>Epidendrum montserratense</i>) from dead trees on the island and installed them in the security of the island's botanic garden.</p>
<p>Montserrat is also home to the critically endangered <a href="/wiki/Leptodactylus_fallax" title="Leptodactylus fallax">Giant Ditch Frog (<i>Leptodactylus fallax</i>)</a>, known locally as the Mountain Chicken, found only in Montserrat and Dominica. The species has undergone catastrophic declines due to the amphibian disease <a href="/wiki/Chytridiomycosis" title="Chytridiomycosis">Chytridiomycosis</a> and the volcanic eruption in 1997. Experts from <a href="/wiki/Durrell_Wildlife_Conservation_Trust" title="Durrell Wildlife Conservation Trust">Durrell Wildlife Conservation Trust</a> have been working with the Montserrat Department of Environment to conserve the frog <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In-situ_conservation" title="In-situ conservation">in-situ</a> in a project called "Saving the Mountain Chicken",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> and an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ex-situ_conservation" title="Ex-situ conservation">ex-situ</a> captive breeding population has been set up in partnership with Durrell Wildlife Conservation Trust, <a href="/wiki/Zoological_Society_of_London" title="Zoological Society of London">Zoological Society of London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chester_Zoo" title="Chester Zoo">North of England Zoological Society</a>, Parken Zoo and the Governments of Montserrat and Dominica. Releases from this programme have already taken place in a hope to increase the numbers of the frog and reduce extinction risk from Chytridiomycosis.</p>
<p>The national bird is the endemic <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_oriole" title="Montserrat oriole">Montserrat oriole</a> (<i>Icterus oberi</i>),.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List">IUCN Red List</a> classifies it as Critically Endangered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Captive populations are held in several zoos in the UK including: <a href="/wiki/Chester_Zoo" title="Chester Zoo">Chester Zoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoological_Society_of_London" title="Zoological Society of London">Zoological Society of London</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jersey_Zoo" title="Jersey Zoo">Jersey Zoo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Zoological_Society_of_Scotland" title="Royal Zoological Society of Scotland">Royal Zoological Society of Scotland</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_galliwasp" title="Montserrat galliwasp">Montserrat galliwasp</a>, (<i>Diploglossus montisserrati</i>), a type of lizard, is endemic to Montserrat and is listed on the <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List">IUCN Red List</a> as Critically Endangered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> A species action plan has been developed for this species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, a biodiversity assessment for the Centre Hills was conducted. To support the work of local conservationists, a team of international partners including: <a href="/wiki/Durrell_Wildlife_Conservation_Trust" title="Durrell Wildlife Conservation Trust">Durrell Wildlife Conservation Trust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanic_Gardens,_Kew" title="Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew">Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_for_the_Protection_of_Birds" title="Royal Society for the Protection of Birds">Royal Society for the Protection of Birds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montana_State_University" title="Montana State University">Montana State University</a>, carried out extensive surveys and collected biological data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-durrell.org_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-durrell.org-36">[36]</a></sup> Researchers from <a href="/wiki/Montana_State_University" title="Montana State University">Montana State University</a> found that the invertebrate fauna was particularly rich on the island. The report found that the number of invertebrate species known to occur in Montserrat is 1,241. The number of known beetle species is 718 species from 63 families. It is estimated that 120 invertebrates are endemic to Montserrat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-durrell.org_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-durrell.org-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>Montserrat is known for its coral reefs and its caves along the shore. These caves house many species of bats, and efforts are underway to monitor and protect the ten species of bats from extinction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>A species of tarantula simply called the Montserrat Tarantula is native to the island. It was first bred in captivity at the <a href="/wiki/Chester_Zoo" title="Chester Zoo">Chester Zoo</a> in August 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caribe_Queen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Caribe_Queen.jpg/220px-Caribe_Queen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Caribe_Queen.jpg/330px-Caribe_Queen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Caribe_Queen.jpg/440px-Caribe_Queen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caribe_Queen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Motor_ship" title="Motor ship">MV</a> <i>Caribe Queen</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a> ferry boat which shuttles passengers between <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a> and Montserrat several times a week.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Montserrat" title="Economy of Montserrat">Economy of Montserrat</a></div>
<p>From 1979 to 1989, Montserrat was home to a branch of <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIR_Studios" title="AIR Studios">AIR Studios</a>, making the island popular with musicians who often went there to record while taking advantage of the island's climate and beautiful surroundings; the studio closed as a result of Hurricane Hugo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AirMonserrat_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-AirMonserrat-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the devastations of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">Hurricane Hugo</a> and the eruption of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soufriere_Hills_Volcano" title="Soufriere Hills Volcano">Soufriere Hills Volcano</a>, the Montserratian economy has been effectively halted. Export businesses based in Montserrat deal primarily in the selling and shipping of aggregate for construction. Imports include virtually everything available for sale on the island.</p>
<p>The island's operating budget is largely supplied by the British government and administered through the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Development" title="Department for International Development">Department for International Development</a> (DFID) amounting to approximately £25 million per year. Additional amounts are secured through income and property taxes, licence and other fees as well as customs duties levied on imported goods.</p>
<p>The limited economy of Montserrat, coupled with a population under 5,000, many living in shelters and shacks without utilities, only consumes 1.7 MW of electric power, produced by five diesel generators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016Pop_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-2016Pop-4">[4]</a></sup> Two exploratory <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_power" title="Geothermal power">geothermal wells</a> have found good resources and the pad for a third geothermal well was prepared in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Together the geothermal wells should produce more power than the island requires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(October 2014)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>As a British Overseas Territory (BOT), defence of Montserrat remains the responsibility of the United Kingdom. Montserrat is one of four of the remaining fourteen BOTs that maintains its own military unit, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Montserrat_Defence_Force" title="Royal Montserrat Defence Force">Royal Montserrat Defence Force</a>. There is also a cadet corps for secondary school students.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Montserrat" title="Demographics of Montserrat">Demographics of Montserrat</a></div>
<p>The island had a population of 5,879 (according to a 2008 estimate). An estimated 8,000 refugees left the island (<a href="/wiki/Montserratians_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Montserratians in the United Kingdom">primarily to the UK</a>) following the resumption of volcanic activity in July 1995; the population was 13,000 in 1994. The 2011 Montserrat census indicated a population of 4,922.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In early 2016, the estimated population had reached nearly 5000 primarily due to immigration from other islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016Pop_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-2016Pop-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Age structure:</p>
<ul>
<li>0–14 years: 23.4% (male 1,062; female 1,041)</li>
<li>15–64 years: 65.3% (male 2,805; female 3,066)</li>
<li>65 years and over: 11.3% (male 537; female 484) (2003 est.)</li>
</ul>
<p>The median age of the population was 28.1 as of 2002 and the sex ratio was 0.96 males/female as of 2000.</p>
<p>The population growth rate is 6.9% (2008 est.), with a birth rate of 17.57 births/1,000 population, death rate of 7.34 deaths/1,000 population (2003 est.), and net migration rate of 195.35/1,000 population (2000 est.) There is an infant mortality rate of 7.77 deaths/1,000 live births (2003 est.). The life expectancy at birth is 78.36 years: 76.24 for males and 80.59 for females (2003 est.). The total fertility rate is 1.8 children born/woman (2003 est.).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Residents of Montserrat are known as Montserratians. The population consists of a number of ethnic groups, including Black (88.4%), White, Dual Heritage and Creole. The island's population is mainly a mix of Irish and Africans with other minorities.</p>
<p>The population is predominantly, but not exclusively, of mixed African-Irish descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freepages.genealogy.rootsweb.ancestry.com_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-freepages.genealogy.rootsweb.ancestry.com-44">[44]</a></sup> It is not known with certainty how many African slaves and indentured Irish labourers were brought to the West Indies, though according to one estimate some 60,000 Irish were "Barbadosed" by <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yale.edu_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-yale.edu-45">[45]</a></sup> some of whom would have arrived in Montserrat.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Montserrat" title="Education in Montserrat">Education in Montserrat</a></div>
<p>Education in Montserrat is compulsory for children between the ages of 5 and 14, and free up to the age of 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_Cultural_Center_(5809290561).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg/220px-Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg/330px-Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg/440px-Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<p>In 1977, Sir <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a> fell in love with Montserrat and decided to build the ultimate get-away-from-it-all recording studio. Opened in 1979, AIR Studios Montserrat offered all of the technical facilities of its London predecessor, but with the advantages of an exotic location.</p>
<p>For more than a decade, AIR Montserrat played host to classic recording sessions by a who’s who of rock, including Dire Straits, Phil Collins, The Police, Sir Paul McCartney, Sir Elton John, Duran Duran, Michael Jackson, Stevie Wonder, Sheena Easton, Ultravox, The Rolling Stones, Lou Reed, Black Sabbath and Eric Clapton.</p>
<p>Then, in 1989, disaster struck when Montserrat was dealt a devastating blow by Hurricane Hugo which destroyed 90% of the island’s structures and brought the studio’s glittering story to an abrupt end.</p>
<p>After the eruption, until his death in 2016, George Martin raised funds to help the victims and families on the island. The first event was a star-studded event at London’s Royal Albert Hall featuring many artists who had previously recorded on the island including Paul McCartney, Mark Knopfler, Elton John, Sting, Eric Clapton and Midge Ure. All the proceeds from the show went towards short-term relief for the islanders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-airstudios.com_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-airstudios.com-47">[47]</a></sup> Martin’s second major initiative was to release five hundred limited edition lithographs of his score for the Beatles song "<a href="/wiki/Yesterday_(Beatles_song)" title="Yesterday (Beatles song)">Yesterday</a>". Complete with mistakes and tea stains the lithographs are numbered and signed by Paul McCartney and Martin.</p>
<p>The lithograph sale raised more than US$1.4 million which helped fund the building of a new cultural and community centre for Montserrat and provided a much needed focal point to help the re-generation of the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-airstudios.com_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-airstudios.com-47">[47]</a></sup> Many albums of note were recorded at <a href="/wiki/Associated_Independent_Recording" title="Associated Independent Recording">AIR Studios</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Dire_Straits" title="Dire Straits">Dire Straits</a>' <i>Brothers in Arms</i>; <a href="/wiki/Duran_Duran" title="Duran Duran">Duran Duran</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Seven_and_the_Ragged_Tiger" title="Seven and the Ragged Tiger">Seven and the Ragged Tiger</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/The_Police" title="The Police">the Police</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghost_in_the_Machine_(The_Police_album)" title="Ghost in the Machine (The Police album)">Ghost in the Machine</a></i> and <i>Synchronicity</i> (the video for "<a href="/wiki/Every_Little_Thing_She_Does_Is_Magic" title="Every Little Thing She Does Is Magic">Every Little Thing She Does Is Magic</a>" was filmed in Montserrat, but the song ironically was the only one on <i>Ghost in the Machine</i> not recorded there), and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Buffett" title="Jimmy Buffett">Jimmy Buffett</a>'s <i>Volcano</i> (named for Soufrière Hills). After sustaining severe damage from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">Hurricane Hugo</a> in 1989, the studio is now a ruin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-airstudios.com_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-airstudios.com-47">[47]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ian_Anderson" title="Ian Anderson">Ian Anderson</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Jethro_Tull_(band)" title="Jethro Tull (band)">Jethro Tull</a>) recorded the song "Montserrat" off "<a href="/wiki/The_Secret_Language_of_Birds" title="The Secret Language of Birds">The Secret Language of Birds</a>" in tribute to the volcanic difficulties and feeling among residents of being abandoned by the UK government.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Montserrat has one national radio station, ZJB. The station offers a wide selection of music and news within the island and also on the internet for Montserratians living overseas.</p>
<p>Notable shows include the Morning Show with Basil Chambers and the Sadie Mac show on Saturday afternoons. DJ Sadie Mac is also famous for presenting 'Sadie's Fit Tips' on the Morning Show which open with "Good Morning Basil, Good Morning Montserrat...".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Montserrat’s national dish is <a href="/wiki/Goat_water" title="Goat water">Goat water</a>, a thick goat meat stew served with crusty bread rolls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016Pop_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-2016Pop-4">[4]</a></sup> Montserrat cuisine resembles the general British and Caribbean cuisines, as it is situated in the Caribbean zone and it is a British territory. The cuisine includes a wide range of light meats, like fish, seafood and chicken, which are mostly grilled or roasted. Being a fusion of numerous cultures, such as Spanish, French, African, Indian and Amerindian, the Caribbean cuisine is unique and complex. More sophisticated meals include the Montserrat jerk shrimp, with rum, cinnamon bananas and cranberry. In other more rural areas, people prefer to eat homemade food, like the traditional mahi mahi and local breads.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">Cricket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cricket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> is a popular sport in Montserrat. Players from Montserrat are eligible to play for the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies cricket team</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jim_Allen_(cricketer)" title="Jim Allen (cricketer)">Jim Allen</a> was the first to play for West Indies and he represented the <a href="/wiki/World_Series_Cricket" title="World Series Cricket">World Series Cricket</a> West Indians. No other player from Montserrat had gone on to represent West Indies until <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Baker" title="Lionel Baker">Lionel Baker</a> made his One Day International debut against Pakistan in November 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montserrat_cricket_team" title="Montserrat cricket team">Montserrat cricket team</a> forms a part of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands_cricket_team" title="Leeward Islands cricket team">Leeward Islands cricket team</a> in regional domestic cricket, however it plays as a separate entity in minor regional matches,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> as well having previously played <a href="/wiki/Twenty20" title="Twenty20">Twenty20</a> cricket in the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_20/20" title="Stanford 20/20">Stanford 20/20</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Two grounds on the island have held <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class</a> matches for the Leeward Islands, the first and most historic was <a href="/wiki/Sturge_Park" title="Sturge Park">Sturge Park</a> in Plymouth, which had been in use since the 1920s. This was destroyed in 1997, by the volcanic eruption. A new ground, the <a href="/wiki/Salem_Oval" title="Salem Oval">Salem Oval</a>, was constructed and opened in 2000. This has also held first-class cricket. A second ground has been constructed at Little Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Surfing">Surfing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Surfing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Surfing was introduced by two American brothers in 1980, Carrll and Gary Robilotta. They were also responsible for naming the surfing spots on the island. Carrll wrote for the surfing newsletter <i>The Surf Report</i>, which was used by surfers around the globe. They both made Montserrat their home for 12 years.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Montserrat has its own <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> affiliated <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_national_football_team" title="Montserrat national football team">football team</a>, and has competed in the World Cup qualifiers five times but failed to advance to the finals from 2002 to 2018. A field for the team was built near the airport by FIFA. In 2002, the team competed in a friendly match with the second-lowest-ranked team in FIFA at that time, <a href="/wiki/Bhutan_national_football_team" title="Bhutan national football team">Bhutan</a>, in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Other_Final" title="The Other Final">The Other Final</a></i>, the same day as the final of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2002_World_Cup" title="2002 World Cup">2002 World Cup</a>. Bhutan won 4–0. Montserrat has failed to qualify for any <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>. They have also failed to ever qualify for the <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Gold_Cup" title="CONCACAF Gold Cup">Gold Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Cup" title="Caribbean Cup">Caribbean Cup</a>. The current national team relies mostly on the diaspora in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and in the last WCQ against <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_national_football_team" title="Curaçao national football team">Curaçao</a> nearly all their squad played and lived in England.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Montserrat has competed in every <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> since 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Basketball is growing in popularity in Montserrat with Montserrat now setting up their own basketball league.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The league contains six teams these are the Look-Out Shooters, Davy Hill Ras Valley, Cudjoe Head Renegades, St. Peters Hilltop, Salem Jammers and MSS School Warriors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> They have also built a new 800 seater complex which cost 1.5 million</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parishes">Parishes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Parishes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="401" data-file-width="264" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg/170px-Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg/255px-Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg/340px-Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Montserrat's parishes: Saint Peter is top, Saint Georges centre and Saint Anthony bottom. The square marks Plymouth, the abandoned capital.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Montserrat is divided into three parishes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Saint Peter Parish</li>
<li>Saint Anthony Parish</li>
<li>Saint Georges Parish</li>
</ul>
<p>The locations of settlements on the island have been vastly changed since the volcanic activity began. Only Saint Peter Parish in the northwest of the island is now inhabited, with a population of between 4,000 and 6,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The other two parishes are still too dangerous to inhabit; the volcano is still active in 2013.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlements">Settlements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Settlements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Little_Bay,_Montserrat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg/220px-Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg/330px-Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg/440px-Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

Little Bay, the site of the new capital. <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_Montserratians">Notable Montserratians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notable Montserratians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jim_Allen_(cricketer)" title="Jim Allen (cricketer)">Jim Allen</a>, former cricketer who represented the <a href="/wiki/World_Series_Cricket" title="World Series Cricket">World Series Cricket</a> West Indians.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jennette_Arnold" title="Jennette Arnold">Jennette Arnold</a>, the first Montserratian elected as a Member of the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a>, who served four terms as Chair of the Assembly.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lionel_Baker" title="Lionel Baker">Lionel Baker</a>, the first Montserratian to represent the West Indies in international cricket.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arrow_(musician)" title="Arrow (musician)">Alphonsus "Arrow" Cassell</a>, musician known for his <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">soca</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Hot_Hot_Hot_(Arrow_song)" title="Hot Hot Hot (Arrow song)">Hot Hot Hot</a>", which sold over four million copies.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Farrell" title="Vladimir Farrell">Vladimir Farrell</a>, association footballer.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Howard_A._Fergus" title="Howard A. Fergus">Howard A. Fergus</a>, author, poet and three time acting <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Montserrat#Governors_of_Montserrat.2C_1971.E2.80.93present" title="Governor of Montserrat">governor of Montserrat</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Patricia_Griffin" title="Patricia Griffin">Patricia Griffin</a> (1907-1986) pioneer nurse and volunteer social worker, honored on a 2006 series of stamps recognizing notable citizens<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_Irish" title="George Irish">George Irish</a>, writer, human rights activist.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/E._A._Markham" title="E. A. Markham">E A Markham</a>, poet and author.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dean_Mason" title="Dean Mason">Dean Mason</a>, association footballer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shane_Ryan_(social_activist)" title="Shane Ryan (social activist)">Shane Ryan</a>, writer, human rights activist.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/M._P._Shiel" title="M. P. Shiel">M. P. Shiel</a>, writer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lyle_Taylor" title="Lyle Taylor">Lyle Taylor</a>, association footballer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maizie_Williams" title="Maizie Williams">Maizie Williams</a>, member of pop group <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boney_M" title="Boney M">Boney M</a>.</li>
</ul>

<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
<div>
<ul>
<li>1. <a href="/wiki/Condominium" title="Condominium">Occupied jointly</a> with the United States.</li>
<li>2. In 1931, Canada and other British <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">dominions</a> obtained self-government through the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster</a>. See <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Canada" title="Name of Canada">Name of Canada</a>.</li>
<li>3. Gave up <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">self-rule</a> in 1934, but remained a <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> Dominion until it <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">joined Canada</a> in 1949.</li>
</ul>

<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">

<li>Since 1658 <u><a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena" title="Saint Helena">Saint Helena</a></u><sup>14</sup></li>

<li>Since 1908 <u><a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Territory" title="British Antarctic Territory">British Antarctic Territory</a></u><sup>15</sup></li>
<li>1841–1933 <i><a href="/wiki/Australian_Antarctic_Territory" title="Australian Antarctic Territory">Australian Antarctic Territory</a></i> <small>(transferred to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Australia" title="Commonwealth of Australia">Commonwealth of Australia</a>)</small></li>
<li>1841–1947 <i><a href="/wiki/Ross_Dependency" title="Ross Dependency">Ross Dependency</a></i> <small>(transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Realm_of_New_Zealand" title="Realm of New Zealand">Realm of New Zealand</a>)</small></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height:2px">
<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
<div>
<ul>
<li>14. Since 2009 part of <u><a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena,_Ascension_and_Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha">Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha</a></u>; Ascension Island (1922–) and Tristan da Cunha (1938–) were previously dependencies of Saint Helena.</li>
<li>15. Both claimed in 1908; territories formed in 1962 (British Antarctic Territory) and 1985 (South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands).</li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">Africa</th>
